<a id="t-47d02448ad"></a>
## Thread: Enterprise Cobol 3.4: How compile all members of a PDS in one step?? — 5 msgs

_Topics: [`Help requests and how-to`](topics.md#help)_

### Enterprise Cobol 3.4: How compile all members of a PDS in one step??

- **From:** zosrothko <zosrothko@orange.fr>
- **Date:** 2009-06-08T16:03:54+02:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<h0j5o9$296o$1@adenine.netfront.net>`

```
Hi

The Enterprise XLC/C++ compiler is able to compile all members of a PDS in only 
one step and I did not found the equivalent functionality for Enterprise Cobol. 
Anybody aware of this point??

May be could it become a extension request to IBM??

zosrothko
```

#### ↳ Re: Enterprise Cobol 3.4: How compile all members of a PDS in one step??

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@nospam.ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2009-06-08T15:31:35-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<JyeXl.69343$fo6.53199@en-nntp-09.dc1.easynews.com>`
- **References:** `<h0j5o9$296o$1@adenine.netfront.net>`

```
If you are a SHARE member, then you could submit this as a SHARE requirement. 
HOWEVER, I doubt that this would get much support.  It would be relatively easy 
to create a CLIST or REXX to do this.  Some of the source management systems 
(e.g. Endeavor or SCLM) may already have this functionality - I don't know.

However, do this should be a pretty unusual thing to need to do.  At least I 
can't think of many times that this would be useful.  It would, also, require 
that you keep your COPY members in a different PDS than your main source code. 
Some shops do this and some don't.

Finally, are you aware that Enterprise COBOL *does* support the compilation of 
multiple sources at one time.  You simply end the first program with an END 
PROGRAM header and then put the next code after it.  This can be done for as 
many programs as you want.
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Enterprise Cobol 3.4: How compile all members of a PDS in one step??

- **From:** zosrothko <zosrothko@orange.fr>
- **Date:** 2009-06-08T22:50:24-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<2be7f465-2c1b-46f0-8547-87c0f0a99542@h23g2000vbc.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<h0j5o9$296o$1@adenine.netfront.net> <JyeXl.69343$fo6.53199@en-nntp-09.dc1.easynews.com>`

```
Hi Bill

>
> However, do this should be a pretty unusual thing to need to do.
So why the Enterprise XLC/C++ team provides this feature and not the
Enterprise Cobol team?? This is incoherent!. This feature is useful
when one needs to package many source files in many packages (one
paxkage == one PDS) without having to know in advance which sources
should go in which package(a maintenability issue). Using one single
step to compile all sources of a PDS without knowing which sources are
in the PDS greatly simplifies the overall JCLs. (one of our
application is more than 10 000 of cobol sources!)

Ok this could be done with CLIST of REXX but this adds unecessary
steps and tools to maintain that would be avoided if the all-members-
compilation feature was available.
 At least I
> can't think of many times that this would be useful.  It would, also, require
> that you keep your COPY members in a different PDS than your main source code.
…[23 more quoted lines elided]…
>
```

## Thread: Computer literacy — 16 msgs

### Computer literacy

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@nospam.ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2009-06-08T15:43:08-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<yJeXl.74005$2p1.36646@en-nntp-08.dc1.easynews.com>`

```
Just a "funny" on this topic.

When I first went to work for a PC COBOL compiler vendor (whose name, Micro 
Focus, shall remain named <G>), I was primarily responsible for "IBM mainframe 
compatibility".  On the first day that I went to work there, I asked if they had 
access to an IBM mainframe with a COBOL compiler and I was told that they did. 
I then asked what operating system they had, and was given the answer:

  PROFS

This answer should be "widely humorous" to IBM mainframers of the 1980's and 
90's and totally incomprehensible to those who didn't work in that environment 
(and who don't search the internet for the reference).

As has been indicated in the other thread, "computer literacy" is a term with 
multiple (situation dependent) meanings.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Computer literacy

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@nospam.ix.netcom.com>

- **References:** `<yJeXl.74005$2p1.36646@en-nntp-08.dc1.easynews.com> <j3ts25ldk7uko7mv0n55p3su5ln4n7o3mo@4ax.com> <msl035huhg4ucak571eg5ak4cc6t12baei@4ax.com>`

```
No, they were not pulling my leg.  Almost none of the workforce used the 
"mainframe" for anything BUT email.  (They didn't even use the PROFS "document" 
feature with SCRIPT for documentation - until I showed them how).

And, yes, the only IBM mainframe compiler they had was under VM/CMS.  I had to 
"refresh" my XEDIT (not to be confused with the Unix/Linux Xedit) knowledge.  I 
also had to install an "add on" SORT and VSAM support to be able to do "basic" 
mainframe compatibility testing.  We even had the "short-lived" CICS/CMS at one 
time, but mostly I did IMS and CICS testing via "time-share".

Later on (before MERANT days), then did get an in-house MVS system.

P.S. "PROFS" made it into (US) national news around the Watergate period of 
time.  There were several White House executives who claimed to be VERY 
surprised that when they "hit send" on email, that it didn't magically disappear 
as soon as someone read it, i.e. that there were backups of all their 
"inappropriate" email notes.  (This was relatively early in the days of "common 
emails for businesses)  Having been a systems programmer at various times, this 
always amused me as I am certain that these were the same people who EXPECTED 
"IT" to be able to "restore" anything that they ever deleted.

There are a few "interesting" news stories on "missing" email from a later 
(still Republican) White House where email backups WERE lost in the 2003-2005 
period of time.  The *claim* was that this was due to a LOTUS (follow-on product 
to PROFS - sort-of) email system to a Microsoft Outlook (or exchange?) system.
```

get lumped into the 'closet' team, the folks who are supposed to keep the

get sent off to classes and then, based on their classwork alone, design, 
code and implement a new system...

... at which point I become the 'closet guy' that folks come to with 'how 
come this isn't doing what I want?'... and *boy*, do they get annoyed with 
a response that begins with 'Well, the assumptions that went into the 
design, from the very bottom, seem to have neglected...'

Anyhow... there have been times when I have Wanted Out and been told by 
the pimp that I can't do that, there's a clause in my contract which 
states if I leave while the client still has work they'd want me to do 
then I have to pay the agency what they would have earned.  My response at 
that point is 'Mr Jones, we can behave like gentlemen and find a way out 
of this... or I can go in to work tomorrow and in obscenity-free English 
tell the Project Director exactly what I think of him, his approach, the 
quality of his personnel... and his little dog, too.  I guarantee that by 
noon you will receive a call demanding my removal from that cite...

... and you will *never* place another consultant with that Director 
again.  How would you like to play this one out?'

DD

Meaning is the result of interpretation, or so Wittgenstein has it... 
granted, that you are not a professor indicates the conditions of tenure 
may not have application to your situation... but that could be another 
story.  Consider, for example, the possibility that the rules governing 
your position are, by contract and law, to be considered to have the same 
force and validity as those rules which tenure has for professors.

The rules governing tenure then change... and thus, by contractual 
application, the rules governing your employ change.  Not being a 
professor tenure (or, more precisely, 'the condition at your particular 
institution referred to as tenure) has an effect on your own situatuation.

>

> professor tenure (or, more precisely, 'the condition at your particular

No, it does not.  Tenure is something offered to Full Professors by
the contract under which they are employed.  I am not covered by
said contract and thus there is no concept of tenure governing my
employment.  As a matter of fact, there is no contract governing my
employment.  We used to have contracts that had to be renewed every
fiscal year but the administration convinced people this was not in
their best interests and they did away with them.  We are now just
regular employees like the guy who hands you your fries at Burger King.

It is actually an intereting situation.  Under the old system they
could get rid of an employee by merely not offering them a new
contract at the beginning of the FY.  Of course, now they can get
rid of you anytime they want because our employment is no longer
contractual in nature.  Not sure which way is better.

bill

- **From:** Michael Wojcik <mwojcik@newsguy.com>

- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol

- **In-Reply-To:** `<79a0o2F1pmibbU2@mid.individual.net>`
- **References:** `<1244473129_7117@bgtnsc06-news.ops.worldnet.att.net> <79792tF1onr6hU3@mid.individual.net> <797h2rF1plh12U1@mid.individual.net> <797qgpF1phf1rU2@mid.individual.net> <h0oh7m$pok$3@reader1.panix.com> <79a0o2F1pmibbU2@mid.individual.net>`

```
Bill Gunshannon wrote:
> 
> No, it does not.  Tenure is something offered to Full Professors by
> the contract under which they are employed.

At most US universities, you do not have to be a Full Professor to be
tenured. Most US universities tenure professors at the Associate
level; promotion to Full comes later, if at all. Tenure is often
granted in conjunction with a promotion from Assistant to Associate,
but there's no necessary connection between the two.

Tenure (again, at the typical US university) is a status that may be
awarded to "tenure-track" professors, as opposed to fixed-term and
adjunct professors. Tenure track is a feature of the professor's
contract; obviously, most professors consider tenure-track jobs more
desirable, because they offer better job security, as well as more
prestige and typically better benefits. In many institutions,
fixed-term and adjunct faculty can't hold various administrative
roles, can't sit on graduate committees, etc.

Tenure-track professors must apply for tenure (the usual idiom is "go
up for tenure"). Typically this happens in their fourth year at the
Assistant level. Most institutions have a "tenure clock" for
tenure-track faculty that requires them to go up for tenure after a
certain number of years on the job; the clock can be temporarily
halted for reasons such as medical leave, and faculty who perform
particularly well can go up early.

You go up for tenure by submitting a file of your qualifications to
the Promotion and Tenure Committee of the department where your tenure
line resides. (Some people have split tenure lines and have to go
before two committees; some people have tenure lines that are owned
elsewhere in the university hierarchy, eg by a non-departmental unit
in a college.) The file - we're probably talking a banker's box or two
of material - demonstrates your work in three areas: teaching,
research, and service (administrative work, work in the field such as
editing journals, etc). The mix of work is expected to hit targets
that vary from university to university and unit to unit; research
universities require more research than do teaching universities, for
example. The file also goes to a couple (or more) outside reviewers,
people in your field at other universities (or retired, etc). They
write letters supporting (you hope) your tenure case; those go into
the file too. And you write your own letter explaining why you deserve
tenure.

The P&T Committee - a handful of people from your department,
typically elected on an annual basis - evaluates your tenure case. In
the old days this would have taken place in solemn secrecy in a
smoke-filled room, but in our enlightened modern age smoking is
prohibited. If they like what they see, they recommend you for tenure.
Your chair conveys this, and your whole freakin' tenure file, to the
college housing your unit. A committee *there* reviews it and if so
inclined pass it on to the Provost's office. The Provost says yea or
nay. At some universities the President also gets a say - notoriously,
at Harvard the President can override everyone else either way, and
sometimes does.

So, 'round about the end of the academic year, you'll find out
(typically back-channel, with a formal announcement a bit later)
whether you were tenured.

Tenure basically means you can't be dismissed from your job for
anything less than a major infraction of university policy or
conviction for a major crime, and even then only after a pretty
complex process is followed. I've seen tenured professors be fired for
sexual misconduct and then successfully sue for their jobs back
because the university didn't follow process. The idea, of course, is
that tenure protects intellectual freedom because tenured professors
can't be threatened with job loss for political reasons; and in fact
it does contribute to the quality and breadth of research. There are
reasons why the US has the best university system in the world, and
the tenure system - for all its flaws - is one of them. (It also helps
universities retain faculty, because getting hired with tenure at
another place is a complicated process.)

If you don't get tenure, there are a couple of possible outcomes.
Sometimes you're allowed to go back up for it next year. Sometimes
your appointment is terminated (typically after another year), and you
have to look for another job. Sometimes you can transition to a
fixed-term appointment or a full-time administrative position, or some
other employment category.

ObOnTopic: I use newsguy (newsguy.com), which is a pay service and not
cheap. It also gives me an email account - easy to come by these days,
but I've had it for years, so I'm loathe to give it up. newsguy is
pretty aggressive about filtering spam, too, so I tolerate the cost.
```

behind my saying 'I have enough trouble dealing with 'what is', let along

Not according to the example I generated.  In said example... the rules 
governing tenure change and this is reflected in a Professor's contract, 
your contract changes not a whit.  HOWEVER... your (possible) contract 
states that you are to be treated in the same manner as granted in a 
Professioral contract in regards to tenure.  The Professorial contract 
changes and the way you are treated - based on the Professorial contract - 
changes in like manner.

This happens in Law, at times, as well.  Code XVII, Section 102, states 
'for the purpose of this section the term 'hingodilinee' is to be 
considered as being in accord with the definition for 'hingdolinee' found 
in Code XIX, Section 86.

Code XIX, Section 86 is then amended to change this definition.  The 
results trickle down to CODE XVII, Section 102, as the definition there is 
predicated on the earlier one.

Likewise, with the hypothetical case of tenure.

>As a matter of fact, there is no contract governing my
>employment.  We used to have contracts that had to be renewed every
>fiscal year but the administration convinced people this was not in
>their best interests and they did away with them.  We are now just
>regular employees like the guy who hands you your fries at Burger King.

... but, one might hope, with slightly better diction.

>
>It is actually an intereting situation.  Under the old system they
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
>contractual in nature.  Not sure which way is better.

That depends, I would say, on the 'for whom' the better is being applied.

##### ↳ ↳ Re: AT&T Usenet Netnews Service Shutting Down

- **From:** SkippyPB <swiegand@Nospam.neo.rr.com>

<a id="t-a3172dbab2"></a>
## Thread: Underscore in datanames — 35 msgs

### Underscore in datanames

- **From:** "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2009-06-10T02:15:56+12:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<79794vF1pep3iU1@mid.individual.net>`

```
I tripped up recently when processing some client source data definitions.

Looked at it for ages and couldn't see a problem, then realised that certain 
fields had been defined with underscores instead of hyphens in the names. It 
looked like a maintenance programmer had made two sets of amendments to a 
very large record definition (Hundreds of datanames, lots of REDEFINES and 
OCCURS, an absolute delight that caused my Toolset to give up and just 
declare "Too many fields".)  I enlarged the Toolset buffers considerably but 
then it gave the same message from ACCESS and SQL Server when the Toolset 
tried to EXECUTE the DDL it had generated, in order to create an equivalent 
RDB table.

It turned out that the underscores were contributing signally to the 
problem. (Various parsers internal in the Toolset just spat the dummy when 
they found these underscores and this caused duplicate datanames, which 
cannot be added to a RDB table and so on...)

Obviously, I fixed up the definition but this means that any applications 
which reference those underscore fields will fail now and will have to be 
globally edited and recompiled.

Can anyone tell me if they use underscores as a matter of course in COBOL 
datanames? I understood that the underscore is NOT part of the COBOL 
standard character set (and wrote my parsers accordingly), but there is at 
least one site where they DO use it and have managed to get away with it. 
(It must have compiled OK. Clue: I'm not sure, but it may be a PR1ME 
site...)

Any comments?

Pete.
```

#### ↳ Re: Underscore in datanames

- **From:** docdwarf@panix.com ()
- **Date:** 2009-06-09T14:33:20+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<h0lrrg$lsv$1@reader1.panix.com>`
- **References:** `<79794vF1pep3iU1@mid.individual.net>`

```
In article <79794vF1pep3iU1@mid.individual.net>,
Pete Dashwood <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz> wrote:

[snip]

>Can anyone tell me if they use underscores as a matter of course in COBOL 
>datanames?

Given that DB2 is not COBOL I would say 'no, my experience leads me to 
conclude that underscores are not used as a matter of course in COBOL 
datanames'.  Evertthing-is-done-with-dashes.

On the other hand... I can readily imagine a site where someone said 'Gee, 
Mom, I'm a Programmer!' and by some obscure mangling of SPECIAL-NAMES an 
ALHPABET or a SYMBPOLIC CHARACTER or something else I rarely deal with 
allowed a_data_name to be as valid as a-data-name.

DD
```

VAX COBOL, now DEC COBOL that runs on VMS (and TRU64 Unix for a while)

Don't know what the standard says about "$" signs and link-time resolved
variables either?

identification division.
program-id. yyy.
data division.
working-storage section.
01 ss$_wasclr pic 9(9) comp value external ss$_wasclr.
01 ss$_wasset pic 9(9) comp value external ss$_wasset.
01  sys_status pic 9(9) comp.
procedure division.
00.
    display "set = " ss$_wasset with conversion.
    display "clr = " ss$_wasclr with conversion.
    call "sys$setast"  giving sys_status.
    call "sys$exit" using by value sys_status.
    exit program.
end program yyy.

>
> Cheers,
>
> Pete.

Cheers Richard Maher

Richard Maher wrote:
> Hi Pete,
> 
…[39 more quoted lines elided]…
> 

In the shop I was, we were first under PR1MOS and we used hyphens (I 
don't remember if underscores were authorized or not). Then when we 
migrated to VAX VMS, we began to use underscores initially for system 
names, especially external symbols. Then we bought a dictionary (CDD) 
and a query language (DTR), but because all other supported languages 
used ONLY underscores and NO hyphens, we decided to support fields with 
underscores because it was compatible with all languages used in the 
shop (COBOL and DTR).

>> Pete.

…[9 more quoted lines elided]…

Bernard

From the Language Reference manual:

The default character set used in forming character-strings and separators 
is shown in Enterprise COBOL basic character set (Table 1 on page 4).

....

Well I was not able to copy/paste that chart, but the underscore character 
was not listed.  I will try to use it in a compile tomorrow and see what 
happens.

```
Pete Dashwood wrote:
> 
> Can anyone tell me if they use underscores as a matter of course in COBOL 
> datanames?

I use hyphens in native COBOL, but I use underscores and/or mixed case
in .NET COBOL, because those names interoperate properly with other
.NET languages.

I am not personally a fan of the underscore (I find it inconvenient to
touch-type on a US keyboard), and prefer CamelCase or pascalCase to
separate words in identifiers, but my .NET COBOL team decided on
underscores as part of our naming convention.
```

#### ↳ Re: Underscore in datanames

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@nospam.ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2009-06-10T23:04:32-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<mn%Xl.152568$jp1.16780@en-nntp-06.dc1.easynews.com>`
- **References:** `<79794vF1pep3iU1@mid.individual.net>`

```
Pete,
  I am JUST starting to read this thread.  Let me give a couple of "definitive" 
answers and then try and read further.

The underscore was NOT a part of the '85 Standard (or its amendments) as a part 
of the "COBOL Character Set".

The underscore WAS added to the COBOL character "repertoire" in the '02 
Standard.

There are a number of COBOL implementations that added the underscore to the 
COBOL character set (as an extension) to the '85 Standard and, I think, a few 
more that have included it as they implement parts of the '02 Standard.  (Micro 
Focus has allowed it for many years - but I don't think it has for the 20 years 
mentioned in another note.  IBM does NOT include it in their Enterprise COBOL or 
IBM COBOL for Windows.  I don't think they do for the iSeries or pSeries COBOL 
compilers - but I am less certain of that.)

In the '02 Standard (and the draft of the next revision), the underscore may be 
used in the same places in user-defined words as the hyphen.

As I recall, at least one vendor (possibly HP - for their NON-Micro Focus COBOL 
compiler) had a "special" meaning for when the underscore was the first 
character of a data name.  (Either it was a system name or an external data name 
or something else.  This was a LONG time ago).

Bottom-Line:
  If you want to handle Micro Focus COBOL, then you need to be prepared for the 
underscore in user-defined names.  Similarly, for other '02 Standard compilers. 
If you are working with only IBM mainframe COBOL, then you don't need to be 
prepared to handle it (yet).  (There is a SHARE requirement to add it.)

  * * * *

I hope this helps and  I will now try and read the rest of this thread.
```

## Thread: AS/400 COBOL question — 5 msgs

_Topics: [`AS/400, iSeries, RPG`](topics.md#as400)_

### AS/400 COBOL question

- **From:** Scott Lindstrom <sclind@gmail.com>
- **Date:** 2009-06-09T13:34:33-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<4dee8382-be83-4a05-9c34-cc823f179afc@s21g2000vbb.googlegroups.com>`

```
My COBOL skills are quite a bit rusty and I have a production problem
that needs solving.  I have an old COBOL program that is our ODBC/SQL
log program.  It makes some references to some fields in library
QSYSINC/ file EZDAEP that must have changed between V4R4 (the last
time the program was compiled) and V5R4 (the release we are on now).

First - I reference these fields:

LIB-NAME OF QZDA-NDB-FORMAT2 (1)
LIB-NAME OF QZDA-NDB-FORMAT2 (2)
LIB-NAME OF QZDA-NDB-FORMAT2 (3)
LIB-NAME OF QZDA-NDB-FORMAT2 (4)
LIB-NAME OF QZDA-NDB-FORMAT2 (5)

This used to work but the copybook now is defined as:

       05  NBR-OF-LIBRARIES                    PIC S9(00009) BINARY.
  *                                   Number of libraries in list
  *    05  LIB-NAME                            PIC  X(00010)
  *                                            OCCURS xxxxx TIMES.
  *                                   Varying number
  *                                   of library names

with LIB-NAME commented out.  How can I readily access the first 'x'
number of occurrences of LIB-NAME (up to 5 of them) so I can move
these fields to the logfile record?

Second - I reference this field:
 SQL-STATEMENT-TEXT OF QZDA-SQL-FORMAT2

which now is defined as:

      05  SQL-STATEMENT-TEXT-LEN              PIC S9(00009) BINARY.
 *                                   Length of SQL Stmt text
 *    05  SQL-STATEMENT-TEXT                  PIC  X(xxxxx).
 *                                   Varying length
 *                                   SQL statement text

Again, SQL-STATEMENT-TEXT  is now commented out.  How I can reference
the SQL-STATEMENT-TEXT?

TIA,
Scott
```

#### ↳ Re: AS/400 COBOL question

- **From:** Scott Lindstrom <sclind@gmail.com>
- **Date:** 2009-06-17T11:00:17-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<da5d1fc9-2b64-446e-8007-6a482126da39@a7g2000yqk.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<4dee8382-be83-4a05-9c34-cc823f179afc@s21g2000vbb.googlegroups.com>`

```
I  rec'd some great help from the COBOL400-L on midrange.com.  For the
archives here are the relative snippets of code:

(working storage:)

05  MY-PTR                         USAGE POINTER.
05  LIBNAME-ARRAY-X.
    10  LIBNAME-ARRAY              PIC X(10)
                                   OCCURS 100 TIMES.
LINKAGE SECTION.

  COPY EZDAEP OF QSYSINC-QLBLSRC.

  01  LIBNAME              PIC X(10).
  01  SQL-STATEMENT-TEXT2  PIC X(4096).

SET MY-PTR TO ADDRESS OF SQL-STATEMENT-TEXT-LEN
   OF QZDA-SQL-FORMAT2
SET MY-PTR UP by length of SQL-STATEMENT-TEXT-LEN
SET ADDRESS OF SQL-STATEMENT-TEXT2 TO MY-PTR

 if SQL-STATEMENT-TEXT-LEN > 0

   if SQL-STATEMENT-TEXT-len > 4096
      move 4096 to SQL-STATEMENT-TEXT-len
   end-if

  STRING TODAYS-DATE SPACE TODAYS-TIME SPACE
        <snip>
        SQL-STATEMENT-TEXT2
         (1:SQL-STATEMENT-TEXT-LEN)
           DELIMITED BY SIZE INTO FD-ODBCLOG-RECORD
    else
     STRING TODAYS-DATE SPACE TODAYS-TIME SPACE
           <snip>
           PACKAGE-LIB-NAME
             OF QZDA-SQL-FORMAT2 '|'
           DELIMITED BY SIZE INTO FD-ODBCLOG-RECORD
    end-if
   end-if
=============================================================================
  MOVE SPACES TO LIBNAME-ARRAY-X

  SET MY-PTR TO ADDRESS OF NBR-OF-LIBRARIES
  SET MY-PTR UP BY LENGTH OF NBR-OF-LIBRARIES
  SET ADDRESS OF LIBNAME TO MY-PTR

  PERFORM VARYING SUB FROM 1 BY 1
      UNTIL SUB > NBR-OF-LIBRARIES
      MOVE LIBNAME
          TO LIBNAME-ARRAY (SUB)
      SET MY-PTR UP BY LENGTH OF LIBNAME
      SET ADDRESS OF LIBNAME TO MY-PTR
  END-PERFORM

STRING TODAYS-DATE SPACE TODAYS-TIME SPACE
       <snip>
       LIBNAME-ARRAY-X
        '|'
       DELIMITED BY SIZE INTO FD-ODBCLOG-RECORD
```

<a id="t-bfa86572a6"></a>
## Thread: The list of INVOKEs — 76 msgs

### The list of INVOKEs

- **From:** "Paul H" <NoSpamphobergNoSpam@att.net>
- **Date:** 2009-06-10T00:59:43-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<4a2f4c02$0$23763$bbae4d71@news.suddenlink.net>`

```
In my search for "INVOKEs" I have annoyed Pete, one of the most knowledgeable people out there.  I hope not.  

He keeps saying there is no list of INVOKEs.  But there must be a list somewhere of the INVOKEs that are inherently supported by Micro Focus Net Express.  

I have NE 3.1 on an XP laptop, with Excel 3.  I also have another laptop with Vista, NE 5.1 and Excel 7.

I have a program that uses many INVOKEs.  Examples from a program that works in both environments:

          Invoke TheWorksheet  "getRange"  using myRange
                                  Returning TheRange
          Invoke TheRange  "setValue" using eut(eux).
          move eu-data-length (eux) to ws-col-width, hdg-len (eux).
          Invoke TheRange "getColumnWidth" returning Col-Width.
          move ws-col-width to col-width.
          Invoke TheRange "setColumnWidth" using by value Col-Width.
          invoke TheRange "getfont" returning theFonts
          invoke theFonts "getBold" returning Cell-bold.
      * set field to bold
          move 1 to cell-bold.
          Invoke TheFonts "setBold" using by value Cell-Bold.

and

           Invoke ExcelClass   "new"  Returning ExcelServer
      * test without visible turned on?
            if pp-display = "Y"
               invoke excelServer  "setVisible"    using by value 1
             else
               invoke excelServer  "setVisible"    using by value 0.
           invoke excelServer  "getWorkbooks"  returning theWorkbooks
           invoke theWorkbooks "Add"
           Invoke ExcelServer  "getapplication" Returning TheApplication
           Invoke Theapplication "getActiveworkbook"
                                               Returning TheWorkbook
           Invoke Theapplication "getActivesheet"
                                                Returning TheWorksheet
and

       finish-spreadsheet.
           move pp-xls-name to ExcelFileName.
           inspect ExcelfileName replacing all ".xls" by "    ".
           inspect ExcelFileName replacing all ' ' by X"00".
           invoke theWorkbook "SaveAs" using ExcelFileName
           invoke excelServer "quit"
           invoke excelServer "finalize" returning excelServer.

This final example creates a ".XLS" with Excel 3, and a ".XLSX" with Excel 7.

I have found this partial list:

invoke MSExcel "new" returning ExcelObject
invoke ExcelObject "setVisible" using by value 1
invoke ExcelObject "getWorkBooks" returning WorkBooksCollection 
invoke WorkBooksCollection "Add" returning WorkBook 
invoke ExcelObject "getWorkSheets" returning WorkSheetsCollection 
invoke WorkSheetsCollection "Add" returning WorkSheet 
invoke WorkSheet "setName" using z"Company 01" 
invoke WorkSheetsCollection "getItem" using by value 1 returning WorkSheet 
invoke WorkSheet "activate" 
invoke ExcelObject "getColumns" using z"A:M"
invoke getColumns "Select"
invoke getColumns "setNumberFormat" using by reference "@" 
invoke getColumns "setNumberFormat" using by reference "0"
invoke getColumns "setNumberFormat" using by reference "$0.00"
invoke getColumns "finalize" returning getColumns
invoke getColumns "AutoFit"
invoke getColumns "getEntireColumn" returning getEntireColumn
invoke getEntireColumn "setHidden" using by value 1
invoke getColumns "finalize" returning getColumns
invoke ExcelObject "getCells" using by value 1 by value 1 returning Cell 
invoke Cell "setValue" using by reference WORK-FIELD
invoke Cell "finalize" returning Cell
invoke ExcelObject "getRange" using z"A1:U2"returning CellRange 
invoke CellRange "Select"
invoke CellRange "getFont" returning Font
invoke Font "setName" using z"Comic Sans MS"
invoke Font "setSize" using by value 36 size 4
invoke font "setBold" using by value 1 size 4
invoke font "setColorIndex" using by value 45 *> orange
invoke CellRange "finalize" returning CellRange
invoke ExcelObject "getRows" using WORK-FIELD returning getRows 
invoke getEntireRow "setHidden" using by value 1
invoke getRows "finalize" returning getRows
invoke WorkBook "SaveAs" using by reference filename by value FileFormat by reference z"password"
invoke WorkBook "Close" using by value 0
invoke WorkBook "finalize" returning WorkBook
invoke WorkBooksCollection "finalize" returning WorkBooksCollection 
invoke ExcelObject "Quit"
invoke ExcelObject "Finalize" returning ExcelObject

These and many more are available without me having to define them in any way - just use them.  Therefore there must be a complete list of INVOKEs that Net Express makes available.

Does anyone know where I can find that list, with information about how each one is used?

Thanks,
Paul
```

#### ↳ Re: The list of INVOKEs

- **From:** Frederico Fonseca <real-email-in-msg-spam@email.com>
- **Date:** 2009-06-10T09:52:08+01:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<0csu255cv7vdhjam6gfpng79ps33qhd00m@4ax.com>`
- **References:** `<4a2f4c02$0$23763$bbae4d71@news.suddenlink.net>`

```
On Wed, 10 Jun 2009 00:59:43 -0500, "Paul H"
<NoSpamphobergNoSpam@att.net> wrote:

>In my search for "INVOKEs" I have annoyed Pete, one of the most knowledgeable people out there.  I hope not.  
>
>He keeps saying there is no list of INVOKEs.  But there must be a list somewhere of the INVOKEs that are inherently supported by Micro Focus Net Express.  
>
>I have NE 3.1 on an XP laptop, with Excel 3.  I also have another laptop with Vista, NE 5.1 and Excel 7.

Paul - as Pete said THERE IS NO LIST OF INVOKES FOR COBOL.

a INVOKE is basically calling a OBJECT and doing something with it -
being it getting a new instance of a object, or executing a METHOD or
setting/getting a PROPERTY.

those METHODs or PROPERTIES vary according to the object - e.g. Excel
will have its own list of methods and properties, Word will have
another list, and for example Farpoint Spread will have a completely
diff set also.


so the so called list of invokes you are looking for is NOT on COBOL,
but rather on the object(s) you are using.
This link will give you SOME of the Excel object model overview - all
info you need is there or around it - but as mentioned before by Pete,
you can also do that if you look at the object browser within Excel
itself.

http://msdn.microsoft.com/en-us/library/aa272268(office.11).aspx

How you adapt the object to be usable by COBOL is another story - in
COBOL you need to do a bit more work than on VB or other languages -
but only because of the way objects are defined in both languages.

But all objects and their methods/collections/events/properties can be
worked in COBOL - you just have to learn how to do them - and once and
for all get into your head that there is NO LIST OF INVOKES suported
by MF. - what you have is a list of things that the Object you are
dealing with has - and for that you look on the documentation of THAT
Object.






Frederico Fonseca
ema il: frederico_fonseca at syssoft-int.com
```

Sorry Frederico. I don't care what PECD wrote THERE IS A COBOL LIST OF 
INVOKES for EXCEL if you are using Net Express. (More accurately, there

Whoops ! Saves me replying to him - I see he has found the demo on Excel 
for himself. MsExcel.cpy is a COMPLETE list of COBOL methods plus 
data-types required to INVOKE Excel. It is an extract taken from M/F 
source using the Type Library Assistant in the IDE. In this case M/F did 
the extract for developers. It is of course only up-to-date as at the 
date of the version of N/E. Paul can probably get all that he wants from 
this copyfile.

Should he wish to be more updated, he has a copy of UE of  N/E V 5.1 (or 
is it 5.0 ?), where he can generate a new MsExcel copyfie - but very 
likely doesn't need to.

Now for Paul - Having seen your example of what your Excel worksheet 
looks like - why did you pick Excel ?

Some 10 - 15 years back MS were flogging their Office Suite as a 'You 
can do it all Mr. End-User'. Yeah if they wanted to sweat it out. It is 
not programming but packaged programming - therefore they probably have 
set limitations, e.g., Richard commented on perhaps 1,024 rows was where 
Excel hiccups - and for real volume stuff Excel may not be the answer.

See, somebody here once suggested you could use MS Word to print 
invoices. I subsequently wrote here that was what I thought I would do 
(actually, print paged reports). Thank God Donald Tees was around at the 
time. "Whoa Jimmy, MS Word may not be able to handle the volume !". I 
suspect he was right.

Paul, take a deep breath before you go any further - and look at the 
following :-

\Merant\Net Express\Dialog System\Demo\CommonContainers\Listview

and load project LVIEW. The whole thing is written in COBOL and Dialog 
System. It gives you an elegant grid table, and you don't have to piss 
around with MS 1234 actually means 12.34 !!!  I don't use Dialog System 
and I do have a couple of qualifiers about using the Listview demo 
sample - let me know your reaction to the demo and then we can pursue it 
privately from there if you like, plus I can ask the M/F Forum about any 
limitations.

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Geriatric farts WAS:Re: The list of INVOKEs

- **From:** "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz>

- **References:** `<4a2f4c02$0$23763$bbae4d71@news.suddenlink.net> <0csu255cv7vdhjam6gfpng79ps33qhd00m@4ax.com> <srUXl.2210$Gn4.111@newsfe10.iad> <4A312B10.6F0F.0085.0@efirstbank.com> <pap435dhgia3t1rb6944dmc6kdnqpiqusf@4ax.com>`

```
Howard Brazee wrote:
> On Thu, 11 Jun 2009 16:04:32 -0600, "Frank Swarbrick"
> <Frank.Swarbrick@efirstbank.com> wrote:
…[15 more quoted lines elided]…
> have enough to live on - and new income goes for them.

You are really fortunate, Howard. (I know that hard work and planning had 
more to do with it than luck, but to even be achieving what you planned 
involves a modicum of fortune.)

Consider these amendments:

 1.  "Have to work". But cannot get a job. The skills you have are largely 
out of date or no longer in great demand, and you are competing with 
energetic young people who are not as desperately driven as you are (the 
young will always survive; in a worst case scenario they can go and live at 
home for a while...)  Days go by, the bills mount up and the situation looks 
hopeless...This undermines your energy and confidenece and becomes a 
dwindling spiral.

2.  "Qualified for a pension, but still working full time, building up the 
retirement." This is indeed a fortunate position to be in. I don't know of 
many companies where they allow this, UNLESS you have specific skills they 
are anxious not to lose (or it would cost them more to replace you, than to 
let you stay on while they train your replacement). In some countries 
retirement is compulsory at retirement age and companies CANNOT (officially 
and legally) do this. (They can get round it by retiring you, then engaging 
you as a contract consultant...)

3. "Retired - any money from work is for toys." Except for those who are 
retired and trying to live on their pensions.  Then "any money from work" is 
used to buy fripperies like electricity, water, and food... :-)

Since I passed 60 (and did NOT collect $200) I have been giving more thought 
to "retirement". I reckon a bank heist could be a good option. The banks 
have all the money, and what's the worst that could happen? You get away 
with it, sweet... You get caught, free heating, clothing, food and lodging 
for a number of years... I can't see a downside, compared to the way some 
retirees are forced to live. I'm just surprised there aren't more geriatric 
criminals... (Maybe difficulty in running, and the need for frequent comfort 
stops are not conducive to a life avoiding the Law...)

Having been a freelance for nearly 35 years now, I'm used to not expecting 
anyone to take care of me and am just thankful that I own my house and have 
no debts. If I don't work, I can't afford to live. (I won't qualify for a 
pension for a few years yet and even if I got it (there is some doubt 
because I have been out of NZ a lot), it would be a very meagre existence.) 
Apart from that, I LOVE my work and I need to do it.

For the last 4 years now I have preferred to stay at home, rather than to 
traipse round the world raising the wherewithal that would enable me to stay 
at home... As a result, my savings have been depleted to the point where I 
decided that action must be taken. I had planned on returning to Europe in 
April to seek consultancy work, but the recession put paid to that. It is 
cheaper to live here than there and if I didn't get work pretty immediately, 
it could cost me a fortune just for accommodation and transport.

Being in one place for a period of time has upsides I had not seen or 
considered. I'm getting involved in the local community and some of this is 
really rewarding (not in terms of money, but money isn't everything...seeing 
kids winning and helping them do things they never thought they could is 
beyond price.  I know that most of you who are parents already know this, 
but I spent most of my life avoiding having children so it was new to 
me...:-))

I am finding that if it is possible to create a home based business, this 
could be an ideal model to take me into retirement. I don't enjoy travelling 
(especially long haul) as much as I used to (although First Class is nice... 
I had occasion to do a 4 hour flight to Melbourne recently and was 
upgraded... it was great. Food, drink, mains power and wireless internet for 
the notebook, and space for my 6 foot frame, not to mention some very 
interesting conversation; I was next to a lady who is  a researcher in stem 
cell technology for a California based company, you can imagine how that 
went... :-)), I just don't look forward to 26 hours in Economy any more...

Web skills are a useful asset and the response to the cobol21 site has been 
more than I expected or hoped for.  (I spent many hours revamping the site 
and I don't consider any of it wasted).There is a genuine growing awareness 
that people need to move off COBOL but it needs to be done sensibly and 
carefully. Through the website, PRIMA is becoming a "centre of competence" 
for things Migration and we recently acquired our first North American 
customer for the Migration Toolset. There has been a good level of 
downloading of the free information I have made available (largely connected 
with the COBDATA Tool and using SQL in COBOL, but there have been requests 
for packs on Migration, which I am working on) and I intend to put more up 
there as soon as I can.

The most popular page on the site has been the one that has a picture of an 
IBM mainframe on it... I think there is a fair bit of nostalgia in the 
people who visit. It is kind of fun to interact with a 35 year old COBOL 
component and compare how it looked in 1974 and how it looks on .NET today. 
If people get some insight into understanding and using component 
technology, even just come to realise what INVOKE does in COBOL, (we have 
seen a lack of that demonstrated in this very thread recently) then I am 
satisfied.

Retirement is different things to different people, and much of it, as 
Howard pointed out indirectly, depends on decisions you take many years 
before it arrives. Most of us in our thirties can't imagine ever being 
"old".  We are indestructible and the future can take care of itself. Then, 
one day, you look in a mirror and realise there is more salt than pepper in 
the beard and hair, and the eyes don't have quite the sparkle they used to, 
yet the person inside is still the same, just wiser, maybe calmer, and more 
experienced. (And, as Doc points out, the memory becomes more porous...:-))

If we are "lucky" (and we do the necessary planning) our retirement can be 
an really enjoyable time, just as Howard is finding.

No, it's not. It's a list of EXCEL methods, objects, etc. Hint: Look at the

interface to, say, CorelDraw?

>there is no list of INVOKEs built into MF NE!

There is no list of INVOKEs built into MF NE. What you can invoke depends on 
what you're interfacing *to* -- Excel, in this case.

most of the 'gentlemen' that post to this newsgroup on a regular basis

you in their 'professional' vocabularies.  maybe i can somewhat because 
i wouldn't know what an 'invoke' was if it bit me in the ass.

first; my background.  i began working with computers in a military 
environment... computers that killed.  i then went into state and 
federal government work... computers that lied and stole.  i finished my 
programming career in manufacturing and wholesaling... computers 
supporting fraud and greed.  i've programmed in more languages and 
utilities than i can remember, with considerable experience with cobol, 
bal, and rpg.

after reading all these posts i still wouldn't know an 'invoke' from a 
'nod'.  but i have learned a thing or two; one being that the authors of 
a thing that has something in it that can be 'invoked' are the ones that 
have created that thing, and are the ones responsible for documenting 
what they have created.

from your line quoted above... '...T\Net Express\B...S\EXCEL\M...' tells 
me that you are looking at 'excel' documentation withing 'net express'. 
  if this is in deed what you are looking for then thank net express for 
including excel documentation with the net express product, but rest 
assured that the documentation there is still the work of excel.

you may have found a 'complete' list of invokes, but it is in all 
likelihood a 'complete' list of invokes for a 'specific' version of excel.

so.  relax.  take a chill pill.  you aren't paying these guys a penny 
for what they are normally paid well for.  they don't work for you so 
you can't fire them.  and you began this thing with a call for 'help'. 
they HAVE (sorry; no way to underline) given you useful information in 
their replies as you will discover in the future.

enjoy the experience.

sss

SeaSideSam wrote:
> Paul H wrote:
>> I just found  "c:\Program Files\MERANT\Net
…[17 more quoted lines elided]…
> first; my background.

Sam, I have separated the following quote from the rest because it is 
absolutely beautiful...  Definitely a keeper :-)

> i began working with computers in a military
> environment... computers that killed.  i then went into state and
> federal government work... computers that lied and stole.  i finished
> my programming career in manufacturing and wholesaling... computers
> supporting fraud and greed.

Priceless!

When I first read it, it simply cracked me up, but then I realised there is 
an eerie element of truth in it...

I've always held fast to the belief that what we do, on balance, makes the 
world a better place. Now I'm wondering if that position is really just 
wishful thinking...a justification for what has been my life's work. I hope 
not. There must be people who have benefited from computer technology 
through research and control systems, at least... maybe it is just the 
commercial stuff that is tainted. But then you can argue that the computers 
are just tools, and you can't hold them any more responsible for the greed 
and fraud than you can hold an axe murderer's axe responsible for mayhem...

I honestly don't know.

I do know I really enjoyed this quote.

I'm not going to recontribute to this thread as I having nothing more to say 
about Paul's invokes. I was surprised that Jimmy Gavan, who does know 
something about Object Oriented Programming, failed to see that his 
statement ironically marked as "to be more accurate" is actually completely 
inaccurate, but, in the scheme of things it doesn't matter.


> i've programmed in more languages and
> utilities than i can remember, with considerable experience with
…[6 more quoted lines elided]…
> documenting what they have created.

Spot on.

It's pretty simple really and has been covered many times by self and 
others: Objects have methods. Things they are able to do, procedures, 
actions, whatever you prefer to call them... ("Behaviours" is a good word, I 
think.) To activate that method from COBOL, you must use the OO COBOL 
"INVOKE" verb. As there is an almost infinite (actually, it is described as 
"boundless"; for every method or class containing methods that you can 
enumerate, I can create a new one... it's a bit like counting, really) 
variety of Classes which have Object Methods, there is an equally boundless 
number of possible "INVOKES" so the idea of a "comprehensive" list of all 
possible COBOL INVOKES (for NE or any other COBOLs) is just silly. You might 
as well have a list of all the possible MOVE statements that can be done 
with IBM COBOL...

When I first grappled with these concepts many years ago, I imagined a 
little guy with a flowing robe and a pointy hat, cavorting in front of the 
system, casting the spell and calling on all his Wizard powers to invoke the 
potent magic that would animate the method he was going to control...

It worked for me. Today I understand it at many more levels, but that is 
still an amusing image which helps me understand why they chose "INVOKE".

The confusion has arisen out of a limited understanding,  some examples that 
were meant to help, not be interpreted as Holy Writ, a pressing desire to 
get a result, and a certain amount of laziness in not being prepared to put 
in some time to understand what is being said. Understandable, saddening, 
but not worth getting unwrapped about.

I honestly hope Paul solves his problem.

>
> so.  relax.  take a chill pill.  you aren't paying these guys a penny
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
> their replies as you will discover in the future.

Good advice. It is only computer programming... :-)

Pete.
```

```

"Paul H" <NoSpamphobergNoSpam@att.net> wrote in message 
news:4a2fe7b5$0$23754$bbae4d71@news.suddenlink.net...
>I just found  "c:\Program Files\MERANT\Net
> Express\Base\DEMO\OLEDEMOS\EXCEL\MSEXCEL.CPY".  I need to look thru it in
…[4 more quoted lines elided]…
>
 <snip>

Before there was OO programming with INVOKE there were subroutines that you 
could CALL.  Did you ever need a list of all the programs that can be 
CALLed?  Imagine trying to find all such anywhere in the world.

With OO programming there are Ojects and they encapsulate (contain) methods, 
some of which (the public ones) can be INVOKEd.  EXCEL provides Objects with 
public methods that you can INVOKE.  These may vary depending upon the Excel 
Version.  Java has Objects with methods that can be invoked.  Likewise Word 
and most programs that were developed via OO programming.  The only part of 
this in  the OO COBOL compiler is the INVOKE, the actual methods are 
provided by the Objects themselves, which may have been written using OO 
COBOL, Java, C++, C# etc.  Your program is invoking methods that are 
external to you program and they are external to the OO COBOL compiler.

It may be possible to make a list of methods that can be invoked for a 
particular version of Excel, but that is far from a list of all methods in 
the world, and those methods are not inherently known to the OO COBOL 
compiler.  You would be better served by learning to use an Object browser 
like the one built into Visual Studio.  That way you can search through and 
find the methods that you need, even when they change in new versions of 
Excel.
```

```
Charles Hottel wrote:
> "Howard Brazee" <howard@brazee.net> wrote in message 
> news:fq6235hhiftapsmims7h3f37ad0ikcl40r@4ax.com...
…[10 more quoted lines elided]…
> are looking for and understand it. 

That doesn't really have much to do with Java itself, though. Java
makes documentation a bit easier for the developer, because it comes
with a mechanism for extracting API documentation markup from the
code; but so do a number of other languages, and external
implementations exist for other languages. And nothing prevents people
from documenting libraries for other languages.

Doxygen doesn't (yet) support COBOL, but I believe I've seen mention
of other documentation-extraction systems that do.

Our .NET COBOL supports Microsoft's embedded documentation markup; I'd
be surprised if Fujitsu's doesn't.

And in any of these cases, the documentation only helps if 1) the
developer wrote it, and 2) you have it. (And, as you noted, if you can
find and understand the relevant bits.)
```

```
Charles Hottel wrote:
> 
> IIRC I think Richard codes HTML documentation in his COBOL programs and has 
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
> WEAVE. 

Yes, but embedded documentation markup, as with Javadoc and Doxygen,
is a far cry from Literate Programming.

We discussed this a bit a while back, in the context of my ATTW
presentation. See [1].

Knuth's use of TeX in his original Literate Programming system (which
did indeed use a pair of programs named WEB and WEAVE) was perhaps its
greatest failing. The output of the system was compilable source and a
lovely typeset document explaining just what it did and how; but the
actual source that a maintainer had to understand was a nightmarish
jumble of TeX macros, completely incomprehensible to anyone who hadn't
memorized TeX syntax.

Two steps forward, one step back...


[1] http://groups.google.com/group/comp.lang.cobol/msg/1b9c5eef57c7756d
```

Yes, even though I have written programs which have produced typsetting

some others.  My editor, ROSCOE, is old and many would say archaic, but the 
line commands "nc" and "na" (note COBOL and note Assembler) greatly speed up 
and ease the creation of embedded program comments.

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: The list of INVOKEs

_(thread depth: 11)_

- **From:** "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2009-06-16T23:00:08+12:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<79pc9sF1rpj0vU1@mid.individual.net>`
- **References:** `<4a2f4c02$0$23763$bbae4d71@news.suddenlink.net> <4a2fdc73$0$23752$bbae4d71@news.suddenlink.net> <gqnv25pka25stud919cso6n9pfhnnq9ibb@4ax.com> <4a2fe7b5$0$23754$bbae4d71@news.suddenlink.net> <studnVrzdoIQz63XnZ2dnUVZ_v2dnZ2d@earthlink.com> <fq6235hhiftapsmims7h3f37ad0ikcl40r@4ax.com> <2K2dnZoIq9yMDazXnZ2dnUVZ_radnZ2d@earthlink.com> <h0u0t818jp@news3.newsguy.com> <dc6dndEbJYHCdq_XnZ2dnUVZ_gmdnZ2d@earthlink.com> <h15r4t02i9m@news5.newsguy.com> <qsidnVcpGIN5Z6vXnZ2dnUVZ_gydnZ2d@earthlink.com>`

```
Charles Hottel wrote:
> "Michael Wojcik" <mwojcik@newsguy.com> wrote in message
> news:h15r4t02i9m@news5.newsguy.com...
…[44 more quoted lines elided]…
> greatly speed up and ease the creation of embedded program comments.

Good Heavens, Charlie, I thought ROSCOE was long gone... :-)

Part of my job back in the days when I worked for IBM in Southampton, U.K. 
was to write ROSPROCs to support our local development. (I copped this job 
because I  was the only one who knew it :-))  Eventually, of course, they 
moved to TSO but ROSCOE served them well for many years.

I'm not sure that there is a big enough demand to write a "documenter" for 
COBOL.(I have considered it on a couple of occasions over the years, but I 
no longer work in that world. Flowcharters and such already exist but the 
ones I've seen can't give a "bigger picture"; it takes a programmer to do 
that. COBOL was designed to be "self-documenting" and, when written well, it 
is.

The automatic documentation produced with languages like Java and C# is 
adequate, provided the actual comments get written, so again, it comes down 
to the programmer.

I think the actual volume of code has a lot to do with it. Small 
encapsulated pieces of code  are much easier to get your head around (with 
or without added documentation) than large monolithic programs with many 
thousands of lines of code. For example, today I was working in some C# I 
wrote 3 years ago. It simply isn't a problem. The toolset lets you set book 
marks and jump around the code to your heart's desire. You hit the 
equivalent of a performed routine in COBOL (it's another method being 
invoked) and you need to check exactly what it does... put the cursor on the 
line, click on the bookmark toolbar icon, then right click and select "find 
the definition" from the pop-up context. Instantly, you are at the routine. 
No scrolling through code or opening other windows, just two mouse clicks. 
Read through the method, amend it if you want to, then click the "go to 
bookmark" icon in the toolbar (there are 2;one forward and one backward). 
Instantly you are back where you started from on the very line that you 
jumped out of. You may never know where the method you went to is located in 
the code (although it is easy to mark if you want to you) and it doesn't 
matter. You can track through a logic path without getting sidetracked by 
having ot search for "out of line" code. Not only can you "find the 
definition" but once you are in that code you can "find all references to 
this code" just as easily. Visual Studio simply rocks and we should have had 
tools like this for COBOL decades ago.

I had some fairly complex changes to make to some stuff (extending some 
existing methods and adding some new ones) and I tried to assess how long it 
would have taken if I was doing it in COBOL. For a start the existing code 
would have been 20 to 30 thousand lines. In C# it is around 6, but you make 
the areas you are not working with invisible, and only open them up when you 
need to. (Another feature of VS 2008). I start off with all methods and 
global variable definitions hidden and just work through what I need. It is 
much quicker and less cluttered than having to have a full listing open all 
the time. (Searches can be configured to search hidden code as well as 
visible.)

It is a combination of much better tools, and much more powerful code 
(requiring much less writing and reading) that improves productivity with 
the new languages over COBOL, at least in my experience. There is a learning 
curve, and some of the concepts are new (plus there are new capabilities 
that simply aren't there in COBOL), and different from the way things are 
done in COBOL, but if you persevere you get round the curve and things get 
written and fixed much more quickly than they used to. It is simply easier 
to find and fix stuff. I enjoy working with C# now about as much as I 
enjoyed working with COBOL for many years, and I cannot deny that I produce 
much more working functionality (and often more complex functionality) in 
less time than I did with COBOL.

Having said all of that I still find myself thinking "EVALUATE" 
nostalgically,when I'm coding "SWITCH and CASE"... :-) Old habits die 
hard...:-)

Pete.
```

<snip>

Well ROSPROCs were pretty cryptic but they have been replaced by Roscoe 
Programming Facility (RPFs) which is much better (more similar to REXX).  I 
maintain some that everyone uses to generate their compile JCL.  Not many 
people know the RPF language and most are not interested in learning it. 
These RPFs are supposed to be replaced by some Dimension's stuff.  They need 
to do that before I retire or I do not know who will maintain the RPFs.

Apparently Java is no panacea or else the contractor consortium developing 
the new, replacement systems is poorly managed.  They put a new subsystem 
into production some months ago.  It was over six months late going in and 
they are having a tremendous amount of problems that need to be fixed.  So 
much so that the development on the new subsystem to replace our existing 
subsystem, which was already well under way, has been stopped and a lot of 
contractors have been layed off.

This is probaly all my fault.  They sent me to a Java class and right after 
that all hell broke lose.  This happened before back around 1992-1993 when 
they were planning to use C++.  I took a C++ class and the next thing I know 
they cancelled everything because they decided they could not afford the 
tiered architecture of Unix servers.  I never understood why they couldn't 
determine that up-front before they started.  Anyway all of this greatly 
increases the chances that I will retire before our system is replaced. 
This might even seem funny except for the billions of dollars that have been 
spent. At one time they had 700 to 800 contractors devopling the new system.

As far as extracting commens/documentation from COBOL programs, I can use 
the command: DELETEX 7 7 /*/  which deletes everything except lines with an 
asterisk in column 7.  When I read Michael's presentation I noticed that he 
preferrs using mixed case letters, but I prefer uppercase letter as it is 
simpler to search for words using ROSCOE.  Of course I can convert all to 
uppercase before searching but I am basically lazy.  I seldom extract the 
comments but I have RPFs that can search all members in a PDS, all members 
in a Librarian dataset or all members in a ROSCOE library for whatever 
string I desire.  This has come in handy on many occasions.

Not your problem really is it? :-) You are doing your job; it seems they may 
not be doing theirs...

I guess you could point it out (in an email, so there's a written record...) 
and that would entirely meet any obligation you could be considered to have.

>
> Apparently Java is no panacea or else the contractor consortium
> developing the new, replacement systems is poorly managed.

Hmmm...   I agree Java is no panacea, but then again, neither is anything 
else. Against poor management the finest technology in the world can end up 
looking inadequate. The poor management MAY be on the part f the Consortium, 
but what about the management at your place? Did they have a clear idea of 
what they wanted and did they specify it properly in a RFP? What checks and 
balances are in place to ensure the performance they are paying billions 
for? My point is that "poorly managed" rarely tends to be on one side... If 
a company or organization is well managed and they go to tender, they will 
pretty soon pick up problems with the contractors, (irrespective of how 
illustrious these contractors may be), if those contractors are NOT well 
managed. I saw a major Insurance company in the U.K. cancel a contract 
(after one year of what was going to be three years) when they realised that 
the household name they had contracted the task to was going nowhere. The 
Insurance company was very well managed and they had independent consultants 
(like me) employed to assist and monitor the contractor effort and make sure 
it stayed on track. It soon became apparent that the contractors were using 
it as a testing ground for their latest software and they were much more 
interested in debugging and enhancing their own packages than in providing 
service to the Insurance company. (In effect, the Insurance company was 
picking up the R & D for the contractors...)

Nothing much was being achieved. There were some frank discussions round a 
table with managers from both sides present and concerns and issues were 
raised, promises were received and everyone went back to work. Two months 
later the promises had all been broken or never kept and the contractors 
turned up to work to find their terminals inaccessible and themselves 
escorted from the premises with all work done remaining the property of the 
Insurance company. (We were able to salvage about 60% of it, so it wasn't a 
total loss, but it cost the company a lot of money. Still, nothing like as 
much as if the fiasco had been allowed to continue.) My opinion of the 
Insurance company was strongly reinforced by their decisive action. A less 
well managed company would have been conned into persisting to the end, and 
probably to extend the contract when  it became apparent that the original 
goals failed to materialize.

>  They put
> a new subsystem into production some months ago.  It was over six
…[4 more quoted lines elided]…
> have been layed off.

If a project is haemorraging cash, it is sometimes necessary to stop the 
bleeding before taking stock. There is always a danger of good stuff being 
discarded with the dross, but often that is an acceptable risk. If proper 
management is in place both of these events should be unlikely.

>
> This is probaly all my fault.  They sent me to a Java class and right
> after that all hell broke lose.
LOL!

…[4 more quoted lines elided]…

Most of us are "lazy" inasmuch as we don't like doing more than we have to, 
but on this occasion I would urge you to make a little more effort :-) 
Michael is right about mixed case; it is definitely more readable. After 
working in mainframe environments where ONLY upper case was available, I 
thought COBOL looked "strange" when written in mixed case, but within a 
couple of weeks I was persuaded otherwise. The old Internet injunction 
("there's no need to SHOUT!) is pretty true at some level for most of us.

>

> desire.  This has come in handy on many occasions.

A feature served by global editing that many a programmer has been very 
thankful for.  In Visual Studio you can find/replace not just in the current 
document, or all the open documents, but all the FILES in the project as 
well (Your call...).It has been a boon on a number of occasions when I 
decided to change a name, or even change an output message that could be 
present in more than one library. Make sure you keep a copy of these RPFs 
for yourself, Charlie. You never know when they may come in handy.

Pete.

In article <scKdne2n2Ko-QKXXnZ2dnUVZ_t-dnZ2d@earthlink.com>,
Charles Hottel <chottel@earthlink.net> wrote:

[snip]

>The consortium is being lead by IBM.

Damnation... didn't think of that one.  If the hardware was IBM then it 
was idiocy upon idiocy, as the software would most likely be written in a 
manner which would require the purchase of more hardward.

[snip]

>Have to do my best to be a good team player.

The eternal question... what is better to have, a 'good team player' 
(which often gets translated into 'a completely interchangeable part that 
is exactly the same as everyone else) or a 'surly, gruff, spawn of a 
female dog who Actually Gets Work Done?'

*That* is decided, usually, by the One Who Signs The Paychecks.  Something 
blew up on a Production Weekend at my present client's site and I was 
called to look into it... turned out that someone changed a JOB card (who 
changes JOB cards? you make a copy of one that works and that's it!) and 
the pre-run before the main run blew up.

I sent out an outraged email detailing my concerns that a system which 
generates paychecks for tens of thousands of people relies, in essence, on 
two geezers with obsolete skills... and the autoreply from my group 
director said 'If something goes Awry, contact Mr A, if something goes 
Badly, contact Ms B, if something goes Really, Really Wrong contact Mr C 
(the director of the Agency)'.

I got called on the carpet for sending an email to Mr C... and then showed 
the chain and the instructions.  *Boy*, did they not like that... but Mr C 
sent me a very nice reply of 'Thank you for bringing this to my attention 
and we will take a Very Good Look at the process.'

(this, of course, can mean 'you done good in tellin' me, lad'... or 
'Security will meet you at your desk for Monday's clean-out')

After that carpet-calling my tech lead said that I was never, ever to send 
an email to anyone above (level) unless I cleared it with him first... to 
which I responded that he did not sign my timesheets and as long as it is 
legal I'll mail the White House if I think that getting tens of thousands 
their paychecks is in danger of failing.

He repeated that I was not to send such emails without his approval... and 
I finally snapped with 'If you have the authority to remove the software 
from my machine or limit the use I can make of it then, by all means, do 
so; until such time - and even after - I will continue to communicate in 
ways that I believe, in good faith, will Get The Job Done.'

A sign of a bad attitude, I know.

DD

I'm a bit surprised you let him rile you, Doc (given your depth of 
experience at dealing with such people) but there are times when job stress 
gets the better of all of us.

I think I might have said something along the lines of: "I really can't 
promise not to mail people when I think the need arises, (freedom of speech 
is an ancient custom in this land of ours, and surely you wouldn't want to 
inhibit proper communication lines in a Business environment?) but I 
understand your concern, and I'll make sure you are copied on everything I 
send above level x. Of course, if you feel really strongly about this and 
seek to have my facilities limited, we could discuss it with Mr. C. he seems 
like a very reasonable gentleman and not at all averse to being kept 
informed."

there are no serious repercussions for you.

Sometimes a HUGE amount of good is done by communicating something important 
upwards. I remember an occasion where I did this by writing a report which 
explained what the problem was, how it had arisen and why it wasn't being 
solved. I sent it to my Boss who was a medium angel, His Boss, who was an 
Arch-angel, and God (who I had only met on a couple of occasions.) Some of 
the Cherubim and Seraphim were miffed because they weren't copied, but I had 
tried talking to them and it made no difference. A Commandment came down and 
the problem was fixed. I didn't think anymore about it. About six months 
later I was beavering away in my cubicle in the bull pen with the other 
cherubs when the phone rang. It was God. I was staggered. God really didn't 
just phone up the hoi polloi for a chat... he explained a situation and 
asked my opinion, he said he wanted the opinion of someone on the shop 
floor, who was not playing company politics and who wouldn't simply tell him 
what they thought he wanted to hear. I gave him my viewpoint and pointed out 
a few things that weren't clear and needed investigation. He thanked me and 
hung up. One of my colleagues asked me who it was on the phone, sensing it 
was important... "Nobody", I said.

But the situation He had outlined was very satisfactorily resolved. Some 
years later I wanted to get a reference from him but was told he had retired 
and was living in the Bahamas... :-) I reckon he deserved it.

Pete.

I'll actually be able to get a job as a manager, could you imagine the 
interview?

As another part of the 'Know Your Enemy' portfolio, though, I'll be versed 
in the latest terminology - 'Who's the Sponsor for this project, anyway?' 
- and just think of the tales I'd have to tell then!

DD

Bingo... in my reply to Mr Hottel I asked if a Big Name was being used; as

training-grounds: a team is sent in with a senior-to-junior ratio of 1:4 
and while the seniors hold off the client's inquiries ('Why can't I get a 
simple listing of our customers by region?'  'That's a goooooooood 
question...') the four juniors are expected to learn the client's business 
on the client's dime.

Drop-off rate for the juniors is usually around 50 - 75%... so by the time 
Things Are Right the Big Name has another senior trained to do the same 
thing at a new client all over again.

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: The list of INVOKEs

_(thread depth: 15)_

- **From:** "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2009-06-18T02:57:56+12:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<79sejmF1sm2r0U1@mid.individual.net>`
- **References:** `<4a2f4c02$0$23763$bbae4d71@news.suddenlink.net> <79pc9sF1rpj0vU1@mid.individual.net> <ubqdnSmHtZouyKXXnZ2dnUVZ_rqdnZ2d@earthlink.com> <79s2q5F1sgi4tU1@mid.individual.net> <h1ar82$sep$1@reader1.panix.com>`

```
docdwarf@panix.com wrote:
> In article <79s2q5F1sgi4tU1@mid.individual.net>,
> Pete Dashwood <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz> wrote:
…[16 more quoted lines elided]…
> given it a name like 'Gresham's Law of Management' or the like.

Before what?  I came to this realization around 1985, based on experience. 
While there are many  Gresham's Law's, ranging from currency ("Good money 
drives out bad money") through the behaviour of certain metals, right up to 
the moral and Ethical behaviour of Corporate Management, (I don't know of 
one called "Gresham's Law of Management") I haven't come across one that 
says: "Bad management rarely tends to be on one side. (Where two parties are 
involved and results are less than satisfactory)"  If  a Mr. Gresham did 
indeed come to such a conclusion before I did, then I can only say that my 
experience gels with his... There is obviously no monopoly on truth.

>
>> It soon became apparent that the contractors were using
…[16 more quoted lines elided]…
> the same thing at a new client all over again.

Yes, a lot of this goes on and not only in IT... There is an argument that 
says if things were "properly managed" they wouldn't get away with it (as in 
the case I quoted).
>
> [snip]
…[4 more quoted lines elided]…
> What's in a name?

Oh yes, I forgot. Thanks Doc. I have had my own private name for them for 
some decades now and I won't reveal it here. Suffice to say that if I am 
required to work on Projects they have a hand in, I charge more. (And 
usually it still isn't anywhere near as much as they are charging...)

I remember a beautiful conversation at a household name American Bank in 
London that may be amusing to relate (and safe, as it happened 30 years 
ago...)

There is a "Progress Meeting" and a number of people are sitting round a 
table discussing how things are going. An "Upper Middle" Bank Manager is 
present and he is saying very little, just listening.

The head Accenturion (1200 english pounds a day when top contract 
programmers were making 50) was extolling the fact that, although certain 
areas of the project were slipping slightly behind, overall it was all going 
to be fine because Himself had designed it and was confident that the design 
was sound and Arthur Andersen would guarantee it.

There had been an unfortunate contremps a few weeks prior when I had 
questioned the fact that the hardware being installed could cope with the 
transaction volumes. Voices were raised, words were said (I was 30 years 
younger and did not have the experience and sheer cunning that passes for 
"tact" I have acquired since... :-) Result was my card was marked as a 
"troublemaker" and my continued presence on the project was hanging by a 
thread. Himself went to my Boss and his Boss and told them I was just a 
contract programmer and He was God Almighty and who were they going to 
believe? I got a rap over the knuckles and decided on a campaign of passive 
resistance instead... I started drawing little caricatures and cartoons (I'm 
not bad at this :-)) leaving them lying around, which amused the team no end 
but made Himself redden and demand to know who was doing it. To their 
credit, no one ratted me out (it wouldn't be "cricket"... I have a very soft 
spot for the Brits...) and although he had a pretty fair idea, he never had 
enough evidence to make an accusation. (If he had, I would not have lied, 
but I probably would have hit him before I left...)

So here I was in this dreadful boring meeting listening to Himself say it 
would all be OK because He was Arthur Andersen. It was just more than flesh 
and blood could stand and, being flesh and blood, I couldn't stand it...

Me: So, the fact that we can never possibly handle the volumes we must, is 
all going to be OK because Arthur Andersen says it will?

Himself: Yes, I explained to you when you raised this before that you are 
wrong and there is no cause for concern.

Me: And is that good old Arthur's opinion also?

Himself: WE are Arthur Andersen.

Me: It's a franchise, isn't it? ANYBODY can be Arthur Andersen if they just 
front up with around 100K. It's just like MacDonalds or Kentucky Fried 
Chicken. How did it become infallible? Despite being "wrong" in your eyes, I 
persuaded the IBM rep, who I think we can agree is not biased either way, to 
run some simulations on the projected transaction volumes which your design 
seems to have failed to take into account. Here are the listings. Would you 
like fries with that?

At this point, the meeting was abandoned and I was taken out and shot. (I 
was actually fired about 15 minutes after this meeting because Himself had 
to go and demand my head...and, on reflection, I probably deserved it.)

I can look back and chuckle now, but it nearly ended my contract career. The 
agency I was working through dropped me like a hot potato and it was several 
weeks before I got another contract through a different agency (who I stayed 
with for years and eventually bought a piece of).

I heard later that IBM had become concerned about the simulation figures and 
they changed the HARDWARE design (it was 3790s, first in the U.K.) to have 
more registers and memory so it had more chance of switching tasks fast 
enough to do the job. It didn't save the project. When they first ran test 
runs they found it just wasn't viable and replaced the lot with DEC Vax...I 
believe it may have been the last job AA ever did at that particular Bank. I 
don't know what happened to Himself and I really don't care.

Pete.
```

```
On Jun 15, 12:55 am, "HeyBub" <hey...@NOSPAMgmail.com> wrote:
> Paul H wrote:
> > I just found  "c:\Program Files\MERANT\Net
…[5 more quoted lines elided]…
> Okay, there is no list of INVOKE's built into MF NE.

Given that the referenced file is a .CPY then the contents may well be
templates for those invokes that MF use in their demo program.

The templates may cater for error checking in the use of the invokes
and the file may document how these are used, but, as far as I
understand it, they do not restrict or limit the use of other methods.

The problem that Paul H has with this seems to be the term 'built
into'. No, neither Excell, nor its methods, are 'built into' MF NE. MF
may have provided some templates, but they are templates to what is
'built into' Excell, and the set of templates may be extended
arbitrarily with other Excell methods, or with other application or
class methods.
```

```
HeyBub wrote:
> riplin wrote:
>> On Jun 15, 12:55 am, "HeyBub" <hey...@NOSPAMgmail.com> wrote:
…[24 more quoted lines elided]…
> work.

That is the nub of the whole problem.

It is in understanding and recognising that INVOKE is just a means to 
communicate with functionality in something. If Paul was familiar with even 
the basics of OO programming and understood what a method is, this 
discussion whould never have been started. He would have realised that his 
COBOL INVOKES are simply activating methods in OFFICE components. (Excel 
shares certain methods with other MS OFFICE products, and the SAME invoke 
might be used against Excel, Word and PowerPoint, for example...).

Not knowing something is not a crime and people who have no interest in OO 
have a right to have no interest in it.

But MISUNDERSTANDING it  (based on looking at some examples and bending them 
to fit what you DO understand), then vehemently insisting that that 
misunderstanding is accurate, is much more problematic. I am reminded of the 
savage first viewing water-skiing. When asked what his understanding was, he 
replied: "Man on stiring chase 'm, but him no catch 'm yet.." You may 
understand what a boat is and you may understand what string and chasing 
are, but that doesn't mean you understand water-skiing.

If some kind person had invited the savage to ride in the boat while the 
skiing was taking place, his understanding would have been much different.

It seemed to me that on this occasion Paul declined the boat ride.

Pete.
```

- **Message-ID:** `<ItRXl.21324$8_3.1294@flpi147.ffdc.sbc.com>`

```
In article <4a2fdc73$0$23752$bbae4d71@news.suddenlink.net>, "Paul H" <NoSpamphobergNoSpam@att.net> wrote:

>I do understand what you are saying.  You are telling me that Excel =
>performs what it is told to do.  And how to find these abilities.

Begging your pardon, but -- no, you *don't* understand.
>
>You are ignoring my statement that MF NE has some number of "INVOKE" =
>actions that it recognizes without my having to define them or write =
>them in VB or whatever!

Nonsense. He didn't ignore that statement -- he explained why it's incorrect.
>
>I showed them to you in my example.
…[7 more quoted lines elided]…
>do!

It most definitely is *not* a MF question, and most definitely *is* an Excel 
question. I'll try -- ONCE -- to explain the situation to you in slightly 
different terms:

"INVOKE" is a generic built-in that's part of many programming languages, used 
to incorporate many different data structures or methods into a program, for 
use in interfacing with databases or other software. *Which* *specific* 
*things* can be INVOKEd depends on what you're trying to interface *to* 
(Excel, in this case), not on what you're trying to interface *with* (MF).
```
